#
#	Copyright (c) 2005,2006,2007,2008 Ingres Corporation
#	All rights reserved.
#
# ADF Function Instance definition data file
#
# This file is the source used to generate a variety of Function Instance
# (FI) data for Ingres's builtin functions.  The output generated from this
# file is:
#
#	The function instance description table (for adgfitab.roc)
#		(one entry per FI, arranged in an order convenient
#		for type resolution and operator-to-FI translation)
#
#	The function instance lookup table (for adgfilkup.roc)
#		(one entry per FI, arranged by FI number, convenient
#		for runtime execution or code generation)
#
#	A bunch of #defines giving various indexes into the FI description
#	table, and counts of FI's per operator (for adfopfis.h)
#
#	The STCODE generator table for function instances (for adgstgen.roc)
#
# This data file is processed by the awk program fi_defn.awk.  (Use nawk on
# Solaris.)  Refer to fi_defn.awk for instructions on how to run it, and how
# to place the results into the various .roc and .h files.
#
#
# Data file structure:
#
# This file is generally structured thus:
#
# group adi-operator-type
#   operator adi-operator
#	fi description (fi implementing that operator)
#	fi description
#	...
#   operator ...
#   ...
# group
# ....
#
# The groups MUST appear in the order: ADI_COMPARISON, ADI_OPERATOR,
# ADI_AGG_FUNC, ADI_NORM_FUNC, ADI_PRED_FUNC, ADI_COPY_COERCION,
# and finally ADI_COERCION.  (This is not quite the order of the #define
# values for the operator types, oddly enough.)
#
# Within each group, the operator ID's must appear in sorted order by
# operator ID.  This means numeric #define value, NOT alphabetical
# order!  You must refer to adfops.h in common!hdr!hdr to get the proper
# operator ID ordering.
#
# All FI's for a given operator must appear together.  Ordering is generally
# not specified.  If some particular order is needed for proper type
# resolution, it should be documented.
#
# ** It is up to you to keep the entries in their proper order! **
#
# As should be obvious by this point, a line beginning with # is a comment
# line, in standard awk-y style.  Blank lines are ignored and can be used
# as desired for clarity.
#
# A FI description entry is a multi line entry which has the
# components:
#	fi		function instance number
#	description	description of fi
#	complement	complement FI id
#	flags		optional FI flags
#	lenspec		FI result length specification
#	workspace	optional workspace size
#	null_preinst	Pre-instruction for nullable data handling
#	result		result data type
#	operands	data type of operands if any
#	routine		FI handler routine
#	stcode		STCODE generation info
#
# After the "fi" entry, the lines can be in any order.
# The fi, description, lenspec, null_preinst, result, and stcode
# entries are required.
# The complement, flags, workspace, operands, and routine entries are
# not required.
#
# fi fi-number
#	Must be the first entry of a FI definition, and gives the
#	ADFI_xxx function instance ID number.
#
# description any-text
#	A short description of the FI, just for documentation.
#	The text is also output in a C comment before the FI definition in
#	adgfitab.roc, to make it easier to find things there.
#
# complement fi-number
#	For comparison FI's, the FI ID of the complement function (i.e. the
#	function to use if the FI operands are reversed).
#	ADI_NOFI if omitted.
#
# flags fi-flags
#	Flags for the adi_fiflags member of the FI description.  This
#	can be any constant expression (e.g. flag | flag).
#	ADI_F0_NOFIFLAGS if omitted.
#
# lenspec lenspec-op fixed-size fixed-prec-scale
#	The lenspec definition for the result of the FI.  At least the
#	lenspec-op (the adi_lncompute member of an ADI_LENSPEC) is required.
#	fixed-size, or both fixed-size and fixed-prec-scale, may be
#	specified for fixed size result lenspecs.
#	Warning! Don't put any spaces in "fixed-size" or "fixed-prec-scale",
#	or you'll confuse the AWK program generator.
#	Anything omitted is set to zero.
#
# workspace ws-length
#	The length (bytes) of a workspace if the FI needs any.
#	Zero if omitted.
#
# null_preinst ade_null_op
#	The pre-instruction to use if operands or result are nullable.
#	(ADE_1CXI_SET_SKIP and its friends.)
#	Specify ADE_0CXI_IGNORE if no null pre-instruction is needed.
#
# result datatype
#	The DB_xxx_TYPE data type of the result.
#
# operands datatype ...
#	The DB_xxx_TYPE data types of the operands.  The number of data
#	types listed is counted and used as the operand count for the FI.
#	If omitted, the FI is a zero operand function.
#
# routine adu [agg-begin agg-end]
#	If the FI has an ADF routine to execute it, that routine is
#	listed here.  (It's usually an adu or adc routine.)  For aggregate
#	functions, two additional routines are needed, for begin and end.
#	If omitted, NULL is stored in the FI lookup table.
#
#	Note that CX execution may choose to execute a FI inline, rather
#	than using the listed routine.  If however no routine is listed,
#	CX execution *must* implement the FI inline in some manner.
#
# stcode stcode-case handler [handler ...]
#	The STCODE code-generation case is listed, followed by one or more
#	handler routine addresses for STCODE execution of the FI.
#	If many handlers must be listed, the entry may be continued with
#	a -- at the end of the line, thus:
#	  stcode STC_GEN_DATA3 _ade_i1_i1_add_i1 _ade_i1_i1_add_i2 --
#			_ade_i1_i1_add_i4 _ade_i1_i1_add_i8 ... etc
#	(I chose -- as being easier to see than the traditional \, and
#	marginally easier to handle in awk.)
#
#	For FI's that resolve to many different handlers depending on data
#	item length, the convention is that the leftmost lengths vary
#	fastest (just as the routines are listed in adehandler.c).
#

#	26-Oct-2008 (kiria01) SIR121012
#	    Corrected VARFI setup for constant folding:
#	    Of the previously marked VARFI functions, some are clear, some
#	    remain and others get marked CHKVARFI. This latter flag allows
#	    for a function to indicate whether it did something to break
#	    the constant nature. For example, str->date is usually constant
#	    but breaks if an operation needs to refer to the real time. In
#	    this case we are now told that the performed operation was not
#	    a constant one and we can treat it accordingly.
#	    All the str->float/decimal/money operations were marked VARFI
#	    because they had decimal point or currency implications. As
#	    coercion to binary form leaves the value in a decimal point
#	    neutral form we treat them as constant. This is not the case
#	    for the conversions to string forms - these have to remain but
#	    this is no great loss as it is often only needed at output
#	    time.
#	    Many of the Unicode<->non-Unicode conversions were marked
#	    VARFI due to the possibilty of unmappable characters. This
#	    only affects conversion out of Unicode so these get CHKVARFI
#	    and the other treated as constant.

#           operators with string vs string added ADFI_1470_VARCHAR_DIV_VARCHAR
#           and ADFI_1471_VARCHAR_MUL_VARCHAR.
#       13-May-2010 (horda03) B123704
#           Removed ADFI_1470_VARCHAR_DIV_VARCHAR and ADFI_1471_VARCHAR_MUL_VARCHAR
#           E_AD2063 need an alternate way. Really only want to select the
#           FI 1466 thru 1469 when one of the data type is money and the other
#           is a string, so these FI have either ADI_F65536_PAR1MATCH or
#           ADI_F131072_PAR2MATCH flag set, meaning that they will only be
#           considered if the appropriate parameter is MONEY.
#	3-jun-2010 (stephenb)
#		Fix ADFI_1457_NVL2_ANY with correct return type and new
#		lenspec. (Bug 123880)
#       15-Jun-2010 (horda03) B123926
#           Add IFNULL FI for LONG VARCHAR and LONG BYTE.
#       01-Jul-2010 (horda03) B123234
#           Increase size of DAY() result to an i4 (to handle days in an interval.
#	14-Jul-2010 (kschendel) b123104
#	    Add ii_true, ii_false to solve outer join constant folding bug.
#	28-Jul-2010 (kiria01) b124142
#	    Added SINGLECHK.
#	12-Aug-2010 (kschendel) b124234
#	    All operators with a LONG result have to be flagged NOTVIRGIN.
#	    Otherwise in a multi-row situation, DMF (dmpe_move) might release
#	    the value temp and the next trip thru the CX errors out.
#	    Asking for NOTVIRGIN is hardly an optimal solution but it will
#	    have to do, until opc / qef / dmf is taught to do a better job
#	    of either LOB temps or temp lifetimes or both.
#	4-Oct-2010 (kschendel) b124535
#	    Remove VARFI from text(all) coercion, any to-text coercions that
#	    need VARFI (actually CHKVARFI) e.g. dec->text have specific
#	    FI's.  VARFI was interfering with constant folding.
#
